    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer13260808940482140115">Tana lives in a world where walled cities called Coldtowns exist. In them, quarantined monsters and humans mingle in a decadently bloody mix of predator and prey. The only problem is, once you pass through Coldtown's gates, you can never leave.<br/><br/>One morning, after a perfectly ordinary party, Tana wakes up surrounded by corpses.   <span id="freeText13260808940482140115" style="display:none">Tana lives in a world where walled cities called Coldtowns exist. In them, quarantined monsters and humans mingle in a decadently bloody mix of predator and prey. The only problem is, once you pass through Coldtown's gates, you can never leave.<br /><br />One morning, after a perfectly ordinary party, Tana wakes up surrounded by corpses. The only other survivors of this massacre are her exasperatingly endearing ex-boyfriend, infected and on the edge, and a mysterious boy burdened with a terrible secret. Shaken and determined, Tana enters a race against the clock to save the three of them the only way she knows how: by going straight to the wicked, opulent heart of Coldtown itself.<br /><br /><i>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</i> is a wholly original story of rage and revenge, of guilt and horror, and of love and loathing from bestselling and acclaimed author Holly Black.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13260808940482140115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/177279-this-does-not-sound-like-the-short-story-i">This does not sound like the short story I just read by the same title and author.. Matilda was the girl&#39;s name. She went to Coldtown to save her bf Julian and a friend&#39;s sister, Lydia. Is this the same story or something new?</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It is something new set in the same place/canon and not too long after the short story's time setting. Characters in this book do briefly mention Mati<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It is something new set in the same place/canon and not too long after the short story's time setting. Characters in this book do briefly mention Matilda at one point as well, I guess to help tie the short story to the book a bit more.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2313408357" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313408357" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313408357?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=best-of-decade">best-of-decade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=dystopian-us">dystopian-us</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313408357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16805733224567601597"><b>Holly Black is my Queen</b><blockquote>
  <i>But if you didn't believe in monsters, then how were you going to be able to keep safe from them?</i>
</blockquote>Tana lives in a world where <b>vampires are no longer creatures of myths. </b> Only Holly Black can take such a worn out trope and breath fresh life into it. <blockquote>
  <i>Even from the beginning, that was the problem. People liked pretty things. People even liked pretty things that wanted to kill and eat them.</i>
</blockquote> And, like any good government, the US immediately <b>banished the "new" citizens to</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16805733224567601597" style="display:none"><b>Holly Black is my Queen</b><blockquote>
  <i>But if you didn't believe in monsters, then how were you going to be able to keep safe from them?</i>
</blockquote>Tana lives in a world where <b>vampires are no longer creatures of myths. </b> Only Holly Black can take such a worn out trope and breath fresh life into it. <blockquote>
  <i>Even from the beginning, that was the problem. People liked pretty things. People even liked pretty things that wanted to kill and eat them.</i>
</blockquote> And, like any good government, the US immediately <b>banished the "new" citizens to concentration camps</b>...well, technically walled cities with a good internet connection. But there is extreme <b>poverty, disease and death</b> for all the humans living inside.<br /><br /><b>And the vamps love it.</b> They use the internet to lure in humans - the downtrodden and the adventure seeking - to join their city and become food. <b>People go in but never out.</b><br /><br />Tana wants none of that but when an accidental encounter leaves her potentially infected, she knows <b>she's going to have to go to Coldtown</b> to protect herself and her family. <blockquote>
  <i>Remember that I’m still a monster. I can listen to you scream and cry and beg and I still won’t let you out.</i>
</blockquote> I love the characters in this book. Tana and her little sister had such a <b>realistic give-and-take </b> relationship. Also, the vampire (Gavriel) was <b>such a refreshing twist</b> - he was just the right mixture of moodiness, insanity and danger. <br /><br />This is my second time through and I enjoyed it just as much as the first. <br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />The book was a 4.5 for me but listening it it - 5.0 - definitely. This is one of my all time fave audiobooks - huge thank you to Christine Lakin for reading this one.<br /><br />I've read a few books that use music in between chapters and I'm normally not a fan. This book just blew me away. The music drifts in and out to build the story. There's haunting melodies, fanfare for the tense moments and <i>gah</i> it just brings the tension and intrigue to the next level.<br /><br />And I really enjoyed listening to the reader's voice. She just had this evocative and electrifying tone. Loved it. She's one of the few female readers that actually rocked it when she read the guy voices.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_619973817" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619973817" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619973817?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=tstl">tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619973817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12115655916078020642"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384931106ra/7028903.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>
  <i>Stop being stupid, [Tana] told herself, even though it was much too late for that. She’d been a hundred kinds of stupid already.</i>
</blockquote>I mean, I can hardly be accused of being excessively judgmental on a character's idiocy when she repeatedly realizes she's being dumb, right? :|<br/><br/>I know that Twilight is standard for the vampire book we love to hate. It's often been the butt of my jokes, and I often find myself mocking Bella Swan for her stupidity. With that said, I would read the Twilight series thre</span>
  <span id="freeText12115655916078020642" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384931106ra/7028903.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>Stop being stupid, [Tana] told herself, even though it was much too late for that. She’d been a hundred kinds of stupid already.</i>
</blockquote>I mean, I can hardly be accused of being excessively judgmental on a character's idiocy when she repeatedly realizes she's being dumb, right? :|<br><br>I know that Twilight is standard for the vampire book we love to hate. It's often been the butt of my jokes, and I often find myself mocking Bella Swan for her stupidity. With that said, I would read the Twilight series three times over before reaching for this book again. Yes, I mock Twilight, but at least it has a plot (however simplistic) that is rational and easy to follow. The writing is nothing special, but it is easy to read and easy to understand. Above all, however we tend to mock Bella, she is at best naive, foolish, completely and utterly clueless and without personality---but at least she's smarter than the incomprehensible pile of TSTL poop that is Tana. <b>I cannot find any sympathy, I cannot find any respect, I cannot find any enjoyment, and I cannot find myself liking a character who behaves in such an astoundingly foolish manner.</b><br><br>Bella may be inactive. Bella is immobile. She is catatonic. Bella waits, while the world revolves around her. <b>However boring Bella is, however irrelevant her character, Bella's actions are still more tolerable than the main character in this book, who, at every turn, has the urge to run headfirst into death.</b><br><br><b>The best thing about this book is the writing.</b> Holly Black is a good writer, the writing in this book is poetic...it runs excessively so at times, but I enjoy that sort of writing, so it didn't bother me too much. What did not work was the plot, and the excessiveness of the book. This book was overly long for the material that it contained. You could have easily removed a good 25% of this book without losing relevant, without losing much of the plot. There was too much needless introspection, too many flashbacks, and memories, and characters' POVs that felt largely irrelevant to the main part of the story.<br><br>The concept of Coldtown was interesting at first, but ended up being a mess with a lot of holes and inconsistencies that my mind could not comprehend. This book's type of vampirism does not break any mold, but it was well-conceived enough. Overall, the reason why I disliked this story is because of the characters. <b>I either hated or disliked every single character, with the majority of my loathing directed towards the main character and her incomprehensible stupidity: Tana Bach.</b> The vampires in this book were uninspired, they're a mix between goth-punk-wannabes, or exaggeratedly suave and evil Lestat/Louis-types of Anne Rice's <i>Interview With a Vampire</i> fame.<br><br><u>Setting</u>: Roughly 10 years ago, the world discovered vampirism because an idiotic vampire's mission to just drink blood from his victims, and not kill them. I think we know enough from zombie movies to know that things don't turn out the way he planned. There's no such thing as a little bite. Before he knew it, hundreds of new (and uncontrollable) baby vampires were formed, who then in turned infected thousands more, and well...in short: tons of people died, and vampires are now a presence in the world. Within the US, there are six Coldtowns, populated by vampire and humans, and those who are Cold (bitten by a vampire but not yet turned, with a ferocious desire for human blood). <b>The concept of Coldtown is a mess, and the existence of vampires as both villains and celebrities doesn't quite work for me.</b> It's the equivalent of having hundreds of thousands of people killed by terrorists, and then watching a reality show titled "The Real Housewives of Osama Bin Laden."<br><br>This world glorifies vampires, who are murderers, at the same time it glorifies the people who hunt vampires (Hemlok: Vampire Bounty Hunter is a popular reality show). <b>Vampires have their own reality show feeds directly from Coldtowns</b>, the world gathers to watch vampires party, dance, go to raves, suck on other people's bloods, chill out in sumptuous beds and making out with each other, dressed in glorious velvet clothes soaked through in blood.<br><br>It doesn't make any fucking sense. <b>Coldtown's population and its rules for entrance and exit are inconsistent and again, nonsensical. It is an interesting concept, poorly executed.</b><br><br>Death is meaningless in this book, because there is so much of it. There is no emotion in seeing a character die, at all.<br><br><u>Summary</u>: Tana Bach wakes up from a party, hung over, in a bathtub, and finds herself surrounded by the corpses of her friends.<blockquote>
  <i>The tan carpet was stiff and black with stripes of dried blood, spattered like a Jackson Pollock canvas. The walls were streaked with it, handprints smearing their dingy beige surfaces. And the bodies. Dozens of bodies. People she’d seen every day since kindergarten, people whom she’d played tag with and cried over and kissed were lying at odd angles, their bodies pale and cold, their eyes staring like rows of dolls in a shop window.</i>
</blockquote>Tana is no stranger to vampires. <b>Her mother was bitten and turned Cold before little 10-year old Tana decides it was a good idea to free her crazy mother from her chains in the basement: result, dead mother, scarred-for-life-but-not-much-the-wiser-from-the-experience 17-year old Tana.</b> The corpses were clearly victims of vampires: they all have puncture wounds. There are blood everywhere. Tana herself might have been bitten. What should she do? Call the police? I mean, THERE ARE A TON OF CORPSES. Call her dad? Run away screaming for help? I would understand if she were to run away screaming for help. According to the government: <blockquote>
  <i>if you do come into physical contact with a vampire, you are legally obligated to report yourself to the authorities. Do not attempt to wait to see if you’ve become infected. Do not attempt to self-quarantine. Call 911, explain the nature of the attack, and wait for further instructions.</i>
</blockquote>What does Tana do?<blockquote>
  <i>Tana started giggling, which was bad, she knew, and put her hands over her mouth to smother the sound. It wasn’t okay to laugh in front of dead people. That was like laughing at a funeral.</i>
</blockquote>Ok, fine. She laughs. It's ok, hysteria is fine. I can understand that.<br><br>BUT THEN. BUT THEN. Tana runs into a chained vampire (who might have been the murderer), and her douche of an ex-boyfriend, who has clearly been bitten and is now Cold. What does she do? <b>Why, FREE THEM BOTH.</b> It's of no importance whatsoever that the vampire (Gavriel) might have been the murderer. It's of no importance at all that the ex (Aidan) may spring on her to suck her blood any minute (which he does, repeatedly). Aaaaaaaaaand off we go to Coldtown!<br><br>And along the way, let's just pick up a couple of twins goth web celebrities with a vampire-centric blog who are just dying (no pun intended) to go to Coldtown and become vampires themselves. They conduct video interviews! They ask Tana about her experience as a survivor of the now-deemed Sundown Tragedy. <b>Tana is going to be Youtube sensation!</b><br><br>And we only have 200 pages to go.<br><br>Fuck me.<br><br><u>The Characters</u>: <b>On a scale of marry-me to you-need-to-be-drawn-and-quartered-and-burned-and-not-necessarily-in-that-order, the characters in this book range from I-want-to-punch-you-in-the-balls to kill-it-with-fire.</b><br><br>All kidding aside, there is not a single main or relevant side character in this book whom I would like, whom I would befriend. I've said it before, I've said it many times before in many books, and I will say it again: I cannot understand how the main character in this book can be so mind-numbingly dumb. <u>Tana</u> KNOWS how dangerous a Cold person is. Her mother literally RIPS her arms apart when little 10-year old Tana somehow felt the urge to be a do-gooder and free her mother from her chains in the basement. Being Cold, having a thirst for blood is like an cocaine addict needing a fix, only 10 times worse because you might actually kill a person and rip their throat out in your desperate need and thirst for human blood. It doesn't matter whom. A Cold person's bloodthirst transcends friendship, love, rationality.<br><br>Tana KNOWS this. She IGNORES it yet again when it happens. Not only does she choose to trust the vampire Gavriel, knowing nothing about him, despite his veiled threats and warnings for her NOT to trust him, she tags along with him and rescue him from his chains anyway. When she learns his true identity, she STILL trusts him. <b>Tana's foolishness, impetuousness, idiotic decision making never, ever stops</b>, and I could not enjoy this book considering she is the main character.<br><br>Not to mention this particularly foolish moment: YOU WANT TSTL? YOU GOT TSTL. LET'S JUST DELIBERATELY BAIT A HUNGRY VAMPIRE WITH BLOOD.<blockquote>
  <i>He bent helplessly toward her.<br>She bit her tongue. Bit it hard, the pain chasing through her nerve endings and alchemizing into something close to pleasure. When her mouth opened under his, it was flooded with welling blood.<br>He groaned at the taste of it, red eyes going wide with surprise and something like fear.</i>
</blockquote>NO! NO! NO!<br><br><u>Aidan</u> is, as Tana admitted, the worst boyfriend ever. He is also the worst ex-boyfriend ever. As a human, he is a waste of air. As her boyfriend, he cheated on her, he flaunts his open flirtation with her, and he doesn't discriminate. Boys, girls, he kisses them all. More than one, more than once. He is a master at mind games. He is a smooth talker, a smooth charmer. Aidan has been bitten by a vampire. Aidan is cold. Tana doesn't learn from her lesson. Aidan is now not just a douchebag, he is a dangerously bloodthirsty douchebag. <b>Before their journey, during their journey, after their journey, Aidan makes repeated attempts to rip out Tana's throat. Tana does nothing but admonish him.</b> All Aidan has to do is smile, say something charming and wittily clever, and Tana will forget all his past wrongs. <b>Tana is a fucking doormat on top of being an idiot.</b><br><br>And then we have Gavriel. The powerful, stunningly beautiful ages-old vampire who inexplicably, suddenly falls for Tana. His reason: she saved him. <b>Gavriel has a penchant for overdramatization. He does not speak so much as make a statement</b>. He opens his mouth to spout such gems of wisdom as: <br><br><i>“Fine, fine, everyone’s fine,” said the vampire, a mad gleam in his red eyes, crossing his arms over his chest as Bela Lugosi did in black-and-white films. “Fine as scattered pieces of sand.”</i><br><br><i>“You bid me to bide, but if I’m to burn, then surely you will let me put that fire to some use.”</i><br><br><i>"I promise I will repay you. [With] jewels, lies, slips of paper, dried flowers, memories of things long past, useless quotations, idle hands, beads, buttons, and mischief.”</i><br><br>Screw you.<br><br><b>Gavriel is at best, pretentious. At worse, a Louis/Lestat combination that never entirely works.</b><br><br>There a a pair of Goth Vampire-wannabe web celebrities and video bloggers who aren't even worth mentioning because they're just so fucking random. <b>The twins, Winter and Midnight (real name Jack and Jen) serve no purpose other than to make Tana into a fucking Youtube sensation.</b><br><br><u>The Romance</u>: There's a hint at a love triangle, and the romance doesn't quite work for me. Beyond the incomprehensible fact that Tana would feel anything towards the waste of air that is her ex, Aidan, her romance with Gavriel is equally implausible.<br><br>And then there is this.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Allow me to explain how my whole life has prepared me for this moment. I am used to girls screaming, and your screams—your screams will be sweeter than another’s cries of love.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>How about you go fuck yourself, Gavriel?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12115655916078020642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1128861030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1128861030" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128861030?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128861030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17329370832488413936">Full disclosure, listened to this on audiobook, as I do more and more these days. <br/><br/>Looking back on the book, I suppose that I'm not really the target demographic. It could be that this is YA, and probably targeted toward young women instead of men. (And by "Targeted" I'm mostly talking about the marketing, rather than Black's writing.) <br/><br/>That said, I really enjoyed it. And it only occurred to me right now as I was sitting down to write about it that this book might not be *for* me, technically. <br/><br/>I f</span>
  <span id="freeText17329370832488413936" style="display:none">Full disclosure, listened to this on audiobook, as I do more and more these days. <br /><br />Looking back on the book, I suppose that I'm not really the target demographic. It could be that this is YA, and probably targeted toward young women instead of men. (And by "Targeted" I'm mostly talking about the marketing, rather than Black's writing.) <br /><br />That said, I really enjoyed it. And it only occurred to me right now as I was sitting down to write about it that this book might not be *for* me, technically. <br /><br />I found it a really take on what has the potential to be a very tired trope - a world where vampires have emerged from the shadows. <br /><br />But I didn't find this cliche at all. Quite the opposite in fact. I found the world very interesting and realistic, and the perspective of the story very personal and emotionally charged. <br /><br />I could see this being made into a great movie as well. I'd be surprised if nobody has optioned it yet. <br /><br />So yeah. Absolutely worth your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17329370832488413936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_417738707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417738707" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417738707?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417738707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4106982040165151585"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>1.5 stars</b><br/>Please note that I didn't manage to read the last thirty pages (approx) because, in short, I just couldn't do it. I feel really sad about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12813630.The_Coldest_Girl_in_Coldtown' title='The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</a> as it was easily in my top five most anticipated books of 2013. Since the end of Black's Curse Worker series, I've been desperate to get my hands on anything and everything she writes and I confess to still loving a good vampire novel when it's being told by a capable author. And I gave this book every chance to turn i</span>
  <span id="freeText4106982040165151585" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>1.5 stars</b><br>Please note that I didn't manage to read the last thirty pages (approx) because, in short, I just couldn't do it. I feel really sad about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12813630.The_Coldest_Girl_in_Coldtown" title="The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</a> as it was easily in my top five most anticipated books of 2013. Since the end of Black's Curse Worker series, I've been desperate to get my hands on anything and everything she writes and I confess to still loving a good vampire novel when it's being told by a capable author. And I gave this book every chance to turn it around. I really did. Because I wanted so badly to love it. I turned every page expecting the wow factor to be just around the corner... and it never was.<br><br>Some people have pointed out the similarities between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10215349.The_Immortal_Rules__Blood_of_Eden___1_" title="The Immortal Rules (Blood of Eden, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Immortal Rules</a> and the goodreads description for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12813630.The_Coldest_Girl_in_Coldtown" title="The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</a>, so I'd just like to clear that up: the books have nothing in common beyond the vampires. This book feels set in a world more like our own, in a future where vampirism has spiralled out of control and become an epidemic. Coldtowns have been set up to house these creatures of the night and humans are forced to exercise caution after night falls... or risk becoming infected or dead themselves. The protagonist is Tana, a teenage girl who carries the guilt of being responsible for her mother becoming a vampire. Sound okay? Yeah, I thought so too.<br><br>To give credit where it's due, the first chapter is excellent. It opens with Tana waking up in a bathtub after a night of heavy drinking and partying. Head banging, she stumbles across the house to discover the horrific fate that has befallen her friends and quickly realises that she could very well be next. The story after that moves at a snail's pace; in fact, one might argue that it is non-existent for the majority of the book. I really do hate a plotless novel. A huge percentage of the book is made up of world-building info-dumps and flashbacks to Tana's childhood and the time when her mother became a vampire. Even when I was 75% through the book, I felt like the story had gone nowhere.<br><br>The most exciting aspect of the novel - and something that might save it for some readers - is Gavriel. Why hello there dark and sexy vamp! Even I perked up for a page during that hot makeout session (what can I say? I'm something of a fangbanger) and, despite what seems to be a typical bad boy vamp cliche, Black does offer several chapters of background story on Gavriel so he becomes more fleshed out than other similar love interests. But I think the constant halting of the non-existent present day story was mostly what ruined it for me. As well as being annoyingly plotless, it didn't flow. They were all meandering about, pretending to be doing interesting things, when suddenly it was like CUT... and in comes the info-dump about Coldtowns and how they came about and CUT... here comes the story of either Tana or Gavriel's past. <br><br>Very little happened in the present of the story beyond Tana and Gavriel going at it like horny little bunnies (I exaggerate, that might have been a better book). In fact, what is the story here? I read somewhere that the ending is really good, so is that when Black gives us the goods and lets us know where she's going with this? Perhaps. But the thing is, I'm really not sorry that I missed it. I did not care where the characters were headed in this book and I do not care what happens in the sequel. Sad times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4106982040165151585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1820034377?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1820034377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2472613015054917013">Vampires are… not so sexy anymore?<br/><br/>Objection! How dare you say such a thing? You know, I used to be so in love with vampires in my #preteenhood—after all, ‘‘The Vampire Diaries’’ was one of the first series I had ever read and I fell hard for it.<br/><br/>After that I read ‘‘Twilight’’ like almost every Edward fan on Earth and after that… I couldn’t stop. I would pick whatever vampire book I found. <br/><br/>But now… It’s not the same thing anymore. Things change. I changed. I feel like I know everything about vampi</span>
  <span id="freeText2472613015054917013" style="display:none">Vampires are… not so sexy anymore?<br /><br />Objection! How dare you say such a thing? You know, I used to be so in love with vampires in my #preteenhood—after all, ‘‘The Vampire Diaries’’ was one of the first series I had ever read and I fell hard for it.<br /><br />After that I read ‘‘Twilight’’ like almost every Edward fan on Earth and after that… I couldn’t stop. I would pick whatever vampire book I found. <br /><br />But now… It’s not the same thing anymore. Things change. I changed. I feel like I know everything about vampires. One of the reasons why witches are my favourite creatures is because their magic is unlimited—you can do so much with it, so really, the two words that I associate with witches are: endless creativity.<br /><br />The two words that I associate with vampires are: blood suckers. I know, sad, sad, sad. But that’s the truth. That’s what they are. Their magic is limited. Their hotness is overrated. And immortality is not something I envy.<br /><br />I might be the problem though. ‘‘The Coldest Girl in Coldtown’’ was published in 2013, and if my memory is functioning properly, vampires were still kind of in vogue back then. <br /><br />I actually picked this up because I thought I missed reading about vampires, but turns out I do not. At all. <br /><br />Holly Black’s lyrical writing is, of course, beautiful. No surprise there. And she does write with dept. Her characters are not one-dimensional. Plus the idea of coldtowns wasn’t so bad, really. <br /><br />I do wish I had read this book a few years ago, when it came out. I think I would have liked it better then. Maybe I’ll come back to it in the future or when I’m 90 and I don’t remember anything about vampires. <br /><br />For now, it’s chao vampires. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2472613015054917013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_633186575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633186575" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633186575?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633186575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8969415666979845195"><b>
  <i>"What are they? Are they diseased or demonic? Are they citizens who have become ill, deserving hospitals and care, as some have argued? Or are they the bodies of our loved ones animated by some dark force that we ought to seek to destroy?"</i>
</b><br/><br/>And here I thought originality was gone from vampire stories! It takes none other than Holly Black to prove me wrong. Coldest Girl in Coldtown is not only unique, it's a fun, exciting story full of horror and blood with a little flair of post apocalyptic. <br/><br/>E</span>
  <span id="freeText8969415666979845195" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"What are they? Are they diseased or demonic? Are they citizens who have become ill, deserving hospitals and care, as some have argued? Or are they the bodies of our loved ones animated by some dark force that we ought to seek to destroy?"</i>
</b><br><br>And here I thought originality was gone from vampire stories! It takes none other than Holly Black to prove me wrong. Coldest Girl in Coldtown is not only unique, it's a fun, exciting story full of horror and blood with a little flair of post apocalyptic. <br><br>Ever since a sudden outbreak of vampirism spread throughout the world, vampires are out and feared; even though they're kept quarantined in gated cities, you're never quite safe from the stray ones. Tana learns how true this is when she wakes up after a party to a house full of dead bodies. As far as book beginnings go this is not one I'll forget any time soon. Tana's tangible fear made this even more engaging. From page one I could tell she would be a protagonist with whom I would connect and enjoy the ride. I was right: Holly has fashioned a fresh and compelling narrative voice in her that persuades you to keep flipping the pages until you realize it's 4am and you're passing out against your will. Though if you've read anything by Holly, you'll know she has a way of shaping characters into real, perfectly flawed, and down to earth individuals; Tana being no exception. She has cracks in her exterior that aren't hidden from us; I love how she giggles in the most inappropriate times. This girl is scarred and broken, and she knows it, but she's also selflessly determined. At the same time this makes us feel sympathy towards the situation she found herself in. A situation that sheer bad luck and a caring heart got her in. <br><br>The characters Tana meet throughout this story all shine with charisma, and the villains with atrocity. The latter are portrayed as sick, bloodthirsty bastards who are conniving and vengeful - exactly what true villains should be. And since the blurb kind of hints at one, I can safely say there is no love triangle in this book. In fact, there is not much romance at all - which I was <i>really</i> ok with. What romance there is is mainly introductory, so I'm thinking we'll get more of it in the sequel (for those romantic at hearts). Either way, I trust Holly to balance it all flawlessly. We did meet the ex-boyfriend mentioned in the blurb who is really just that: an ex-boyfriend - if I even want to call him that; I still giggle at the kind of relationship they had. Gavriel is the one who steals the hearts in this book (probably even figuratively). I wasn't sure of him at the beginning, but by the end I was won over! <br><br>After the thrilling first half, the story does slow its pace. I never found myself losing interest, however, as it let characterization and world building shine through. The story is told through Tana's point of view, but we do get treated to a few glimpses of her sister's as well which is great to get an idea of how the story is moving outside this Coldtown. Then we get few flashes from the past that tells the heartbreaking story of Tana's childhood, as well as the history of vampires - simultaneously explaining the reason behind the "apocalypse". I found this incredibly interesting. The vampire lore itself is awesomely unique and scary with their 80 days crazy inducing "infected" period. I was also fascinated - and terrified - by the Coldtowns. Think of them like uncontrolled dog pens. How Coldtowns are active online as a sort of popularity contest gives them an aura of mystery, awe, and power. Thus, people are drawn to them, not knowing they're not nearly as glamorous as they seems from the outside. Poor, unsuspecting humans! <br><br>Also, the twist: Awesome!<br><br>Utterly original and completely badass, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown brings back classic vampires in this tale of revenge, love, and death.<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8969415666979845195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18208714611672689261" style="display:none">3.5/5<br /><br />Not bad! I'm glad that I finally got around to reading this as it's been on my shelf for FOREVER. I really enjoyed the beginning of this book, but towards the middle it slowed down and I began to lose interest. The concept of vampirism in this book was also sort of confusing to me, with "the cold" and how you don't necessarily have to become a vampire if you get infected. I'm used to the straightforward "get bitten, become vampire" type of thing and this world with coldtowns and whatnot unfortunately kept me from getting completely into the story. Also, I listened to an audiobook version, which I should have learned by now that it's not my thing. I usually dislike the narrator (like in this case, the voice never matches up with what I imagine the voices being) and it's easy for me to zone out and miss big events. Despite all of these negatives, I did really enjoy the writing style and the action and I loved how it was just one novel instead of a trilogy. What a breath of fresh air!</span>

<div id="review_655831770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655831770" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655831770?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655831770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer391995413786151870"><b>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</b> was a deliciously creepy and dark story, one that made my heart race and thrill.<br/><br/>Tanna lives in a world that seems not too far off from our own; a time when vampires are no longer myth but present and a threat. These vampires have been contained in our modern world into cities, Coldtowns, guarded but connected by live feeds, blog posts and news stories. Sensationalized and romanticized, but Tanna knows the darker side of the story. She has a sad, frightening tale of i</span>
  <span id="freeText391995413786151870" style="display:none"><b>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</b> was a deliciously creepy and dark story, one that made my heart race and thrill.<br /><br />Tanna lives in a world that seems not too far off from our own; a time when vampires are no longer myth but present and a threat. These vampires have been contained in our modern world into cities, Coldtowns, guarded but connected by live feeds, blog posts and news stories. Sensationalized and romanticized, but Tanna knows the darker side of the story. She has a sad, frightening tale of infection gone horribly wrong in her family’s past. <br /><br />When we meet up with Tanna, she’s like any normal seventeen year old spending her summer at parties and having fun. This all comes to an end when she wakes up to a horrific scene, after she spent the night knocked out from drinking too much. Now she’s on the run with her ex-boyfriend, Aiden, and a boyishly handsome vampire, Gavriel, trying to make it to one of the Coldtowns before Aiden fully changes. <br /><br />This was a dark, mesmerizing story, littered with gore and horror. Holly Black does not hold back painting beautiful and yet terrifying tale. I loved every uneasy minute. <br /><br />Tanna was an easy character to latch onto and root for as she wakes up, and everything is basically full throttle ahead from there on out. She’s determined to do what’s right and yet stay human. Her bizarre and powerful connection to Gavriel surprises and thrills her at the same time. She knows he’s capable of monstrous acts, has probably committed them, but at the same time she sees what he is underneath. <br /><b>
  <i><br />"Tana's heartbeat seemed to have moved into her whole body and thrilled it with a single speeding pulse. Everything was a little blurred at the edges and she wanted---she wanted him to feel like she did, like he'd done something forbidden…"<br /></i>
</b><br />The romance in this story was perfect, and not overwhelming, yet enough to speed your heart rate up in whenever Gavriel and Tanna are together. The thing about a romance that’s not in your face is that you spend time analyzing every move and glance, and every word spoke, until what you suspect and hoped for is confirmed! <br /><br />This story has some twists and revelations, and danger at every turn. I think it was a perfect balance of plot and characterization! I was reminded a little of Sunshine by Robin McKinley (one of my favorite vampire stories) while reading this and I think it was because the way it portrayed vampires, a little strange and alien, fascinating and terrible at the same time. Somehow the relationship between Tanna and Gavriel felt similar, too. Can’t put my finger on exactly why, but I loved it! <br /><br />Fans of horror will love this creepy, unsettling and romantic story!! <br /><br /><i>A copy was provided by Little, Brown Books for Young Readers in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!<br /><br />*Quote taken from an uncorrected proof and may change in the final copy.</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/07/review-giveaway-coldest-girl-in.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="391995413786151870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer14765224858479378394">3.5/5 stars<br/>I'm torn because I really loved Holly Black's writing in this book, but the story still felt too rushed and put together for me. There was lots of insta-love and the characters didn't really get developed - Tana did a bit, but barely. I can understand the rushed feeling because it is a standalone paranormal book - which there are hardly any of - but I've read some great standalones that aren't rushed and include some great character development - I just think this one could've been be</span>
  <span id="freeText14765224858479378394" style="display:none">3.5/5 stars<br />I'm torn because I really loved Holly Black's writing in this book, but the story still felt too rushed and put together for me. There was lots of insta-love and the characters didn't really get developed - Tana did a bit, but barely. I can understand the rushed feeling because it is a standalone paranormal book - which there are hardly any of - but I've read some great standalones that aren't rushed and include some great character development - I just think this one could've been better!<br />Overall it wasn't a bad book, I definitely enjoyed reading it, but it wasn't one of my favorites and didn't blow my mind.</span>

<div id="review_2547308415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2547308415" />
    <a title="Mara YA Mood Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57637124-mara-ya-mood-reader"><img alt="Mara YA Mood Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601241106p2/57637124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2547308415?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara YA Mood Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara YA Mood Reader" href="/user/show/57637124-mara-ya-mood-reader">Mara YA Mood Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57637124-mara-ya-mood-reader?shelf=autumn-reads-halloween">autumn-reads-halloween</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57637124-mara-ya-mood-reader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57637124-mara-ya-mood-reader?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57637124-mara-ya-mood-reader?shelf=halloween-tbr-2018">halloween-tbr-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2547308415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9355198811105123341">I never thought I’d ever read another YA vampire book again. But I’d also never read Holly Black’s YA vampires. And Holly Black’s vampires are freaking vicious and vengeful and gory and felt more real (like if this were to actually happen in real life, I could see it being like this), and much more true to legend. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587424845i/29328018._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><s>I don’t know what made me pick this up after having sworn off vampires years ago.</s> (it was PhantomRin's amazing fanart). I was so over them that I’d literally role my eyes anytime I hea</span>
  <span id="freeText9355198811105123341" style="display:none">I never thought I’d ever read another YA vampire book again. But I’d also never read Holly Black’s YA vampires. And Holly Black’s vampires are freaking vicious and vengeful and gory and felt more real (like if this were to actually happen in real life, I could see it being like this), and much more true to legend. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587424845i/29328018._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>I don’t know what made me pick this up after having sworn off vampires years ago.</s> (it was PhantomRin's amazing fanart). I was so over them that I’d literally role my eyes anytime I heard about yet another bleeding vampire book like, “uuiuugh, people are STILL reading vampire books???!! Whhhhy???” <br>But maybe I was feeling Halloweenish this October and was looking for scarier books (I’m not a horror fan I prefer paranormal) so that’s how I ended up here. And I’m so glad I did. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587425353i/29328044._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’ve had a hit and miss experience with Holly Black and had almost given up on her after <i>Tithe</i> and <i>The White Cat</i> but then <i>The Cruel Prince</i> came out and changed all that. Even so I was hesitant to pick up The Coldest Girl but I did. <br><br>And it just hit alllllllllllll the spots. <br><br>Hit all the spots like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2387007320" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Darkest Part of the Forest</i>
</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981546605" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Cruel Prince</i>
</a> (must reads!!!! Easily 5 stars there as well!) <br><br>If horror is your thing there are bits of it here. Ugh it grossed me out. I hate that gory horror stuff but it really set the dark tone of the book and these nasty vampires and made the story richer. And if it’s not your thing like me, there’s not enough of it to skip this one. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587424845i/29328019._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I especially loved how <i>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</i> was not a romance-driven plot! It’s rare in YA, although it’s starting to become more common just recently (yes!) it makes the story just so much more awesome. I always feel like using romance in these types of books, in excess, is like a cheap shot at building a dying plot. So when it’s not there you get so much more than eye-rolling, played out insta-love and dry-humping scenes. <br><br>I mean we MAY get a dry-humping scene in here still though so don’t worry! There’s still a sprinkle of hotness in here somewhere *creepy perv smile* <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587424845i/29328020._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Which reminds me, do yourself a favour and go check out @phantomRin on IG. The fanart of Gavriel is amazing. The fanart for the other characters too! Actually now I know what turned me on to this book! It was those amazing depictions by @phantomrin! This has happened to me in the past actually....<br><br>Anyway<br><br>Thank you Holly Black for this yet another unputdownable, amazing, dark and naughty and creepy and pretty much perfect YA book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9355198811105123341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15230310452873748610">I've been on a Holly Black binge lately, reading all her books. Pissed at myself for not starting this journey farther back. But we can't turn back time, now can we? So, vampires are hit or miss for me when it come to books. I mainly dig the blood thirsty movie kind.<br/><br/>As for characters, I loved Tana! In pretty much all the vamp books I've read, I've pretty much come across annoying female leads. And thank goodness, she was not. Oh, and Gavriel, you are just the cutest piece of chocolate I ever did</span>
  <span id="freeText15230310452873748610" style="display:none">I've been on a Holly Black binge lately, reading all her books. Pissed at myself for not starting this journey farther back. But we can't turn back time, now can we? So, vampires are hit or miss for me when it come to books. I mainly dig the blood thirsty movie kind.<br /><br />As for characters, I loved Tana! In pretty much all the vamp books I've read, I've pretty much come across annoying female leads. And thank goodness, she was not. Oh, and Gavriel, you are just the cutest piece of chocolate I ever did see!<br /><br />When it came to Lucien and Gavriel, I totally got Lestat and Louis vibes!!! Loved that! It was pretty cool that every other chapter was sort of flashbacks or other characters. Gave the book a little more depth! Let me just say as of right now, I will definitely read anything this woman writes!<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12602147238905704736"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>I freaking loved this book! I am going to buy this for sure! I haven't read a vampire book such as this one yet. It was unique and the storyline was terrific! <br/> <br/>Tana wakes up in a house with dead teenagers all around her. She had went to a part with her ex-boyfriend Aidan. He had been bitten and strapped to a bed, he was also in a room with a very old/young vampire named Gavriel. So you can imagine that Tana was just a wee bit freaked out. <br/><br/>She has to break them</span>
  <span id="freeText12602147238905704736" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br /><br />I freaking loved this book! I am going to buy this for sure! I haven't read a vampire book such as this one yet. It was unique and the storyline was terrific! <br /> <br />Tana wakes up in a house with dead teenagers all around her. She had went to a part with her ex-boyfriend Aidan. He had been bitten and strapped to a bed, he was also in a room with a very old/young vampire named Gavriel. So you can imagine that Tana was just a wee bit freaked out. <br /><br />She has to break them all out and go on a road trip to Coldtown where vampires are kept in a kind of commune. Humans can go there as well to live with them. If your infected and not turned yet then you go there too.<br /><br />They pick up a brother and sister along the way. They were doing an online story about vampires and wanted to go to Coldtown to be changed into vamps. They were going to record all of this for everyone to see as well. They called themselves Winter and Midnight. I liked the fake names :) <br /><br />They make it there and not everything or everyone is who they say they are and things turn into a cluster. But it is sooooooo good! I absolutely loved it. <br /><br />I would recommend to anyone that loves vampire stories and wants to read something a little different. <br /><br />I also developed a crush on Gavriel! :) I wish the author would write a sequel to this book. As far as I know there isn't one, but I can always hope right? <br /><br />Fin</span>

    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713933320?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713933320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14803154456665119856"><b>
  <i>“And I have feelings for you, too. Big, weird, crazy feelings.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I have mixed feelings about this book, but overall I liked it.<br/><br/>Tana was an okay character, and it was valiant the way she didn’t leave a vampire behind to his fate! Even if the decision was likely to kill her!<br/><br/>The storyline in this was alright, although it reminded me quite a bit of ‘The Immortal Rules’, which is probably in part because I found the pace in both of them quite slow. But otherwise – dystopian setting, slightly differ</span>
  <span id="freeText14803154456665119856" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“And I have feelings for you, too. Big, weird, crazy feelings.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I have mixed feelings about this book, but overall I liked it.<br /><br />Tana was an okay character, and it was valiant the way she didn’t leave a vampire behind to his fate! Even if the decision was likely to kill her!<br /><br />The storyline in this was alright, although it reminded me quite a bit of ‘The Immortal Rules’, which is probably in part because I found the pace in both of them quite slow. But otherwise – dystopian setting, slightly different take on vampires, female lead who gets turned into a vampire (to some extent), vampires live in a city and use the human population for food? I totally got the same feeling from both of these. Although I think if I was picking sides I’d say that this was slightly better.<br /><br />There was a little bit of romance, and I didn’t dislike it, even if it was a little unexpected!<br /><br />The ending to this was okay, and it wasn’t too cliff-hanger-y. I’m going to be generous and give this 3.5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14803154456665119856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Noura Khalid (theperksofbeingnoura)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura"><img alt="Noura Khalid (theperksofbeingnoura)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597777380p2/28683811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548155656?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noura Khalid (theperksofbeingnoura)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noura Khalid (theperksofbeingnoura)" href="/user/show/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura">Noura Khalid (theperksofbeingnoura)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316213110" href="/book/show/17333763-the-coldest-girl-in-coldtown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura?shelf=2018-reading-list">2018-reading-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548155656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9025897310083904196"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538814284i/26408489._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“Every hero is the villain of his own story.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I made it my job to read every Holly Black book on the face of this earth. And what could be better than Holly Black and Vampires? damn, this book was good. I say this a lot but this was so incredibly different!<br/><br/>Vampires and modern technology. I mean imagine sitting in the comfort of your home and watching shows about Vampire hunters, Vampire wannabes and Vampires trying to lure you to the dark side. Crazy right? Truthfully, I really missed Vampire</span>
  <span id="freeText9025897310083904196" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538814284i/26408489._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Every hero is the villain of his own story.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I made it my job to read every Holly Black book on the face of this earth. And what could be better than Holly Black and Vampires? damn, this book was good. I say this a lot but this was so incredibly different!<br><br>Vampires and modern technology. I mean imagine sitting in the comfort of your home and watching shows about Vampire hunters, Vampire wannabes and Vampires trying to lure you to the dark side. Crazy right? Truthfully, I really missed Vampire books. It has been such a long time since I’ve picked one up. The storyline was pretty simple but the twist at the end was quite intriguing. The writing is especially loved. and the morbid quotes at the beginning of each chapter (yes I know what you’re thinking)<br><br>I really liked Tana. I loved how she managed to be a complete badass throughout the entire book. She clearly didn't wait for anyone to save her from anything. She did all the saving. Including saving a Vampire which confused me a whole lot. Why would you even do that? but then again Tana is just weird like that.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Even from the beginning, that was the problem. People liked pretty things. People even liked pretty things that wanted to kill and eat them.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Gavriel was completely insane. There’s no better way to describe him. Vampires are psychos and this guy wasn’t very far. I mean he was sweet and he had his moments. Honestly, I laughed so much when it came to him.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“You are more dangerous than daybreak.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Aidan was strange. He was so weird when he became a Vampire. I suppose the crazy caught up to him. Winter and Midnight weren't my favorites if I’m honest. I just thought they were insane. Clearly everyone in this book was. Aside from how weird everyone was I pretty much enjoyed the book. It was slow paced but it didn't bother me. I think I was just really in the mood for this book. I ended up finishing it in 2 days.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9025897310083904196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1475752277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18357675737954598384">It's rare that I come across a vampire book that I so thoroughly enjoy. The Coldest Girl in Coldtown was absolutely phenomenal and I adored it! It was such an interesting take on vampires, quite unlike any other book I've read with them. The world building was fantastic and I just loved the whole idea of the book. And as usual, Black brings to life characters that you can't help but fall completely in love with. The main character Tana is gutsy and doesn't let anything get in her way and I just </span>
  <span id="freeText18357675737954598384" style="display:none">It's rare that I come across a vampire book that I so thoroughly enjoy. The Coldest Girl in Coldtown was absolutely phenomenal and I adored it! It was such an interesting take on vampires, quite unlike any other book I've read with them. The world building was fantastic and I just loved the whole idea of the book. And as usual, Black brings to life characters that you can't help but fall completely in love with. The main character Tana is gutsy and doesn't let anything get in her way and I just adore her. And then we have Gavriel. What is there to say about him other than he is officially my favourite and I love him to pieces. My only complaint about this book is that it's over and I desperately wish there was a sequel!</span>
