<div id="review_994431574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/994431574" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/994431574?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994431574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15582278717584721564"><b> Oh wow. </b> I haven't read a lot of vampire books, but this is <i>completely</i> different to what I've tried. I adored this! At times I was dubious...there were sections that made me think I wasn't going to rate it high. But then -- BOOM -- the beautiful writing, the epic ending, the horrible backstory. I'M SOLD. But in all honesty: this needs be a movie. It would be fabulous. <br/><br/><b> I admit! I was pretty dubious for the first 50%. </b> I didn't understand a lot of the reasonsings behind the plot. So it felt weak</span>
  <span id="freeText15582278717584721564" style="display:none"><b> Oh wow. </b> I haven't read a lot of vampire books, but this is <i>completely</i> different to what I've tried. I adored this! At times I was dubious...there were sections that made me think I wasn't going to rate it high. But then -- BOOM -- the beautiful writing, the epic ending, the horrible backstory. I'M SOLD. But in all honesty: this needs be a movie. It would be fabulous. <br /><br /><b> I admit! I was pretty dubious for the first 50%. </b> I didn't understand a lot of the reasonsings behind the plot. So it felt weak to me, and I also worried that I'd misread things because they didn't make sense. BUT DON'T WORRY. That aaaall sorts out. I got my answers. It became crystal clear. <b> It's turning into the kind of book that grows on you. The more I think about it, the more I realise I loved it. </b> Just get past the initial, "So you wanna run the plot be me again, luv?" feeling. <br /><br /><b> The writing is gorgeous. </b> It really reminds me of Cassandra Clare's writing actually. It's HUGE on the details, but they're make the world real and you can see and taste it. Which is a bit scary in this book, because everything is covered in blood. Blood everywhere. Yay. Vampires. But seriously, if you're dubious about vampires but LOVE epic world-building, then this is for you. I'd say the writing style is the strongest part. <br /><br /><b> The characters? I wasn't so keen on. </b> Our narrator is Tana. I liked her. But I struggle to describe her character to you. She was tugged along by circumstances, but definitely brave and capable. Just maybe a little unrelatable to me. (Totally could be just me though.) Gavriel is the psycho vampire she rescues. (That actually confused me SO much why she helped him. Why was he tied up? Why would she help him? What the --??!) I guess to sum Tana up you'd say: rescuer. And what I loved about her is <b> she could rescue herself. </b> Gav took a while to grow on me, but he was insane. I like insane characters. <br /><br /><b> I also loved the death quotes (omg, that sounds bad) at the beginning of each chapter. </b> I'm not sadistic! I swear! I just...they were interesting, okay?<br /><br /><b> I feel really inspired after reading this! </b> Like I want to go write something epic and urban fantasy! Or I want to make my own writing worlds strong and more detailed. That's how I know I've read a good book. It makes <i>me</i> want to improve my own storytelling abilities. <br /><br />What I had a problem with, though was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lucien and Gav. I didn't really get them. It wasn't until the end of the book where it told how Gav had been so brutally tortured and that's what broke his mind, that I GOT why he was a bit weird. Everyone called him insane, but I didn't really feel it <i>so</i> much until the end. After all, he does drop out of the book for a huge while. I didn't get his and Lucien's relationship for a while...frenemies? And I did NOT understand who/what the Spider was. This is all why it didn't get 5-stars, but I'm pretty sure this is just me and my brain not catching on very fast.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also: <b>The last chapter is my very, very favourite. </b> This quote is. the. best: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <i> He reached into the bag and drew out an odd array of manga, ripped paperbacks of books both classic and modern, and a small stack of crumpled magazines. "See, I even brought some things to read aloud. I wasn't sure what you'd like, so there's a bit of everything.” </i>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="15582278717584721564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_292123303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292123303" />
    <a title="Brad Sells" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3365948-brad-sells"><img alt="Brad Sells" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578588259p2/3365948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292123303?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad Sells" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad Sells" href="/user/show/3365948-brad-sells">Brad Sells</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=arc-own">arc-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365948-brad-sells?shelf=ala-2013">ala-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292123303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3520889073413733394">The Coldest Girl in Coldtown is a unique and utterly fantastic take on vampires, with haunting and beautiful prose + a one-of-a-kind story. Easily a new favorite book of all-time!<br/><br/>Let's go ahead and address the elephant in the room: vampires? They've been used so many times, it's gotten quite old. But luckily, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown gives vampires a fresh and original spin - it's unlike anything I've ever read. And you know what I loved the most about these vampires? They're beautiful (thei</span>
  <span id="freeText3520889073413733394" style="display:none">The Coldest Girl in Coldtown is a unique and utterly fantastic take on vampires, with haunting and beautiful prose + a one-of-a-kind story. Easily a new favorite book of all-time!<br /><br />Let's go ahead and address the elephant in the room: vampires? They've been used so many times, it's gotten quite old. But luckily, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown gives vampires a fresh and original spin - it's unlike anything I've ever read. And you know what I loved the most about these vampires? They're beautiful (their skin is described like marble in the book) and stunning to see, but they are truly monsters at their core. And Holly Black didn't hold back with the scary and terrifying scenes. I adored absolutely every single minute of this book. It's a true and shining gem.<br /><br />The Coldtowns themselves are so awesome, yet freakishly eerie. Once you're in, there's no going back. And woah. I would love to see this novel on the big screen, simply for the reason to the see the Coldtown brought to life. Black's imagination is so vivid and lush (I thought the Curse Workers trilogy was great; The Coldest Girl in Coldtown blew it out of the water.), and she never held back on anything. There are loads of surprising and jaw-falls-open moments. The Coldest Girl in Coldtown will shock you, shake you, and never let you go. Plus side? You'll never want it to end.<br /><br />That. Ending. I can't even compute what happened. Talk about a page-turner! While everything about this novel is awesome, the last 100 pages had me on the edge of my seat and looking behind my back - no joke. And this novel struck a chord with my paranormal side. I have never read a book like The Coldest Girl in Coldtown, but oh man, I adore this book to pieces. One of my favorite reads of the year... and of all-time!<br /><br />And I'm sorry, but I have to talk about these vampires again! Vampires turn many people off immediately, since they've been done so many times. But trust me, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown is <b>an absolute must-read</b> - I cannot even stress that enough! Come September, run to your bookstore and pick up this magnificent new prize in YA. Eerie, chilling, and wholly captivating, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown is one of the best books I've read in a long time.<br /><br />Overall, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown is mind-blowing and phenomenal in every way possible. This shattering new novel will have you in its captivating clutches and leave you begging for more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3520889073413733394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_482839413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482839413" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482839413?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      February read for Rated YA-MA group
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dark-or-taboo">dark-or-taboo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482839413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17739669157868918316">Holly Black is one of those authors who I struggle with when it comes to putting her style of writing into a category. She's a little bit dark, a little bit snarky, and I get the distinct impression that she's going to write what she wants, the way she wants to, and screw anyone who doesn't like it. <br/><br/>Because of this, I have both a love and frustration with her work. Every time I pick up a book of hers, I read it and get caught up in the story. However, every time I pick up a book of hers, I find </span>
  <span id="freeText17739669157868918316" style="display:none">Holly Black is one of those authors who I struggle with when it comes to putting her style of writing into a category. She's a little bit dark, a little bit snarky, and I get the distinct impression that she's going to write what she wants, the way she wants to, and screw anyone who doesn't like it. <br /><br />Because of this, I have both a love and frustration with her work. Every time I pick up a book of hers, I read it and get caught up in the story. However, every time I pick up a book of hers, I find myself annoyed with at least one of the characters; usually it's the lead female or one of the "sidekicks." Out of the five books I've read from this author, I've always found myself drawn more to the lead males than the females <i>every single time</i>, and it has nothing to do with their sex appeal. It's just that generally the male leads tend to have more dimension to them than the females do. And what is up with these side characters who seem to be weird ass parodies of people? In <i>Tithe</i>, it was Corny (that name still kills me). With this book, it was the strangeling twins (although the way their story ended was a sickeningly good shocker). <br /><br />In some way, I feel like I'm doing a disservice to Black's kick-ass style of writing by not rating higher. This chick is a natural-born idea machine. She's also quite clever with her character banter and interaction. But outside the fabulous-ness of the Curse Workers series (which holds a special place in my heart), I find myself closing the pages of a Holly Black book ready to move on, no matter how much the story entertained me.<br /><br />Where I give Black serious credit is with her bravery to write evil and gore in a genre saturated with a romanticized version of what vampires should be. Heads were rolling, blood was spurting, and the body count piled up. It would have been great to see the author just run with it and make this more of an actual horror story, instead of a romance with some dark elements. <br /><br />If you're new to Holly Black and would like to try out her writing, I'd recommend to start with her Curse Workers trilogy. I have a certain fondness for Cassel and his mafia style family who can destroy a person with the touch of an ungloved hand. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17739669157868918316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11065796046697015580">I LOVED this book! I listened to the audiobook and the narrator did an amazing job. There isn't much new or fresh in the way of vampire lore here, but I thought it was an exceptionally well done vampire story. I loved Black's exquisite writing and excellent characterisation, which gave the story a feel of both modern and gothic decadence and decline.   <span id="freeText11065796046697015580" style="display:none">I LOVED this book! I listened to the audiobook and the narrator did an amazing job. There isn't much new or fresh in the way of vampire lore here, but I thought it was an exceptionally well done vampire story. I loved Black's exquisite writing and excellent characterisation, which gave the story a feel of both modern and gothic decadence and decline. For me, it struck exactly the right balance.<br /><br />I see that my GR friends are a bit divided on this one. I think if you are someone who really likes vampire books, you will enjoy this. It's an excellent addition to the genre.</span>

<div id="review_344708494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344708494" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344708494?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=paranormal-other">paranormal-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344708494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7702784240817151627"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"If she was going to die, she might as well die sarcastic.  She'd seen a lot of old movies, and that was definitely the way to go out."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Every time I think I'm done with vampire books, my favorite authors pull me back in with their own twist on this paranormal creature.  Unlike <i>The Immortal Rules</i>, which I've seen this book compared to on occasion, <i>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</i> occurs in a more present-day setting, not years from now when the vampire epidemic has already reduced the huma</span>
  <span id="freeText7702784240817151627" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"If she was going to die, she might as well die sarcastic.  She'd seen a lot of old movies, and that was definitely the way to go out."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Every time I think I'm done with vampire books, my favorite authors pull me back in with their own twist on this paranormal creature.  Unlike <i>The Immortal Rules</i>, which I've seen this book compared to on occasion, <i>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</i> occurs in a more present-day setting, not years from now when the vampire epidemic has already reduced the human population to nothing.  There are five major Coldtowns set up across the US, where vampires and those who have <i>gone cold</i> -- who've been infected by a vampire's bite -- are sent to spend the rest of their days in order to keep the rest of human civilization safe.  Humans must also take extra precaution after nightfall because all of the usual vampire stigmas are present in this novel: sunlight is a no-no, holy water and stakes will kill them, and, of course, <i>they vant to suck your blooooood</i>.<br /><br />Anyway, I received a review copy from the publisher, but after enjoying the Curse Workers series on audio so much, I decided to download the audiobook for <i>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</i>.  A search on Audible showed me that I've never listened to Christine Lakin narrate a novel because this is the only one listed under her name, but I would definitely give future audiobooks narrated by her a chance.  She presented Tana in such a matter-of-fact way, much the way I envisioned her:  direct and to the point.<br /><br />Tana's situation is very different.  She's been bitten before and survived.  So when an attack at a sundown party -- which sounds like a terrible idea to me, when vampires are running rampant -- results in a small bite on her leg, she has faith that she can fight the infection again.  I rather love the self-deprecating character, the one who's humble and never gives up no matter how the odds are stacked against them. Much like Cassel Sharpe in the <i>Curse Workers</i> series taking on ruthless mobsters, Tana ends up taking on some of the most powerful vampires she could ever cross paths with.<br /><br /><i>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</i> is Tana's journey to the Coldtown in Springfield.  She hopes to wait out the infection there, along with her ex-boyfriend Aidan who has gone cold after the attack at the same party where Tana was infected.  Along the way, they meet a vampire and an amateur blogger/filmmaker brother and sister duo, all headed in the same direction.  It was the vampire Gavriel that captivated me the most. Give this girl a hottie with a Russian accent, especially one who seems to be channeling Dimka, and you have a fan for life.  (Not that I wasn't already a super fan of Black's other work.)<br /><br />I loved the background we get on each of the characters as the story progresses, though I did wish this information would have been provided as dialogue between characters rather than flashbacks.  Whenever one of these flashbacks would occur, the transition between character perspectives was hard to decipher on the audio without some sort of heading preceding them.  Though, that's not to say that these flashbacks didn't provide valuable insight into the characters and their motivations.  I could have done without Pearl as a character on the whole, but her presence was necessary in order for that ending to play out the way it did. And so I can also see why it was necessary to include her present-day perspective at times, despite how boring it might have been.  I just didn't much care for what was going on outside of Coldtown at the time.<br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised by that ending.  It wasn't perfect, but it was fitting for these particular characters.  I really hope this remains a stand-alone.  I'm left with a sense of satisfaction that I read another vampire book that <i>might</i> just revitalize this overdone creature and make me love vampires again.  Maybe.  For now, I like that this book showed both sides of vampires:  sexy and glamorous but also dangerous and sadistic.  In other words, fun to read about, but I hope I never truly cross paths with one.<br /><br /><br /><i>Thanks to Little, Brown BFYR &amp; Netgalley for providing a review copy.</i><br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/09/audiobook-review-coldest-girl-in.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7702784240817151627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_631553589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/631553589" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430689841p2/8769426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/631553589?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=physical-arc">physical-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=bea13">bea13</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631553589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14233664545583533722"><a href='http://www.nosegraze.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/coldest-girl-coldtown-feature.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423936i/844925._SX540_.jpg' alt='The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black - I believe she gets to pick the weapon. I hope she picks me.' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b><a href='http://www.nosegraze.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nose Graze</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br/><br/><strong><em>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</em> is haunted and addictingly disturbing!</strong> This book starts off with a bang, and I promise it's a sign of what's to follow. It's dark, gruesome, and gory. After that, I'll admit that it took me a little while to get fully into the story, but once I did, OH MY WORD!!!<br/><br/><blockquote>"They'll drink up the whole world if we let them."<br/><cite>Page 92</cite>
</blockquote><br/><br/><em>
  <strong>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</strong>
</em> takes on an insanely horrifying vibe. <strong>There's lots and lots of blood, brutal</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText14233664545583533722" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.nosegraze.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/coldest-girl-coldtown-feature.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423936i/844925._SX540_.jpg" alt="The Coldest Girl in Coldtown by Holly Black - I believe she gets to pick the weapon. I hope she picks me." class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b><a href="http://www.nosegraze.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Nose Graze</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br><br><strong><em>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</em> is haunted and addictingly disturbing!</strong> This book starts off with a bang, and I promise it's a sign of what's to follow. It's dark, gruesome, and gory. After that, I'll admit that it took me a little while to get fully into the story, but once I did, OH MY WORD!!!<br><br><blockquote>"They'll drink up the whole world if we let them."<br><cite>Page 92</cite>
</blockquote><br><br><em>
  <strong>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</strong>
</em> takes on an insanely horrifying vibe. <strong>There's lots and lots of blood, brutal deaths, and terrifying scenes.</strong> These vampires aren't like the ones in Twilight where they try to not be monsters... these vampires are bloodthirsty, brutal, and have no mercy. Every time I thought something was so crazy and so vile, I figured, <em>"Well this is it. This is the most creepy and violent scene of the book, there's no topping that."</em> But I was proven wrong every.time. Because Holly Black always topped it.<br><br><blockquote>"Every day since the one he'd died was not one where he aged, but rather one where he grew away from humanity. He didn't seem older than he must have been when he died; just entirely stranger."<br><cite>Page 147</cite>
</blockquote><br><br>Things just get more and more twisted, dark, and terrifying, until I couldn't look away. It's like when there's an accident on the freeway and you CAN'T. NOT. LOOK. It's horrible, it's sad, but you can't not look. This is the same thing. <strong><em>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</em> is all kinds of twisted, with bloodbaths, murders, and no happily ever afters.</strong> Sometimes in books I think, <em>"Well these characters obviously won't die."</em> There is no feeling like that in <em>
  <strong>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</strong>
</em>. Holly Black has no mercy and that's what makes this book terrifyingly realistic. There are VAMPIRES out there so there will be many deaths and they will be brutal as hell.<br><br><strong>There's also a really unexpected (or expected, however you look at it) romance that develops, that had me HOOKED!</strong> It's the ultimate kind of dangerous, forbidden love. But it's not cheesy. I kind of couldn't figure it out, but that's why it was so awesome! The whole relationship was so unexpected—the way they acted, the things they said.. everything. But it wasn't unexpected in the way that it doesn't work. Quite the opposite. It worked, and it was so sweet, but it kept you on your toes.<br><br><blockquote>"You are more dangerous than daybreak."<br><cite>Page 160</cite>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>Above everything else, <em>The Coldest Girl in Coldtown</em> is exploding with bloody originality.</strong> I'll admit that I haven't read a ton of vampire books, but this one was so different from everything I thought to expect in one.. and I <em>
  <strong>loved</strong>
</em> it! It's dark, twisted, wrong, and so addicting!! What I love most about this book is how it caught me by surprise. I didn't expect to love it nearly as much as I did, and I kind of love it when that happens!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14233664545583533722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17406279-the-coldest-girl-in-coldtown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794619094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12633773003623560196">Holly Black,<br/><br/>I don't know why I haven't read more of your stuff! I've read only The Darkest Part of the Forest before this one, a year or two ago, and really liked it, so I'm not sure why it's taken me this long to pick up another of your books. My mistake! I loved the flawed characters in this one, the depth of the worldbuilding without info-dumping, the creativity. Also, thanks for making sure you put representation into your book. Some people might call it "the liberal agenda," but I'll gladly</span>
  <span id="freeText12633773003623560196" style="display:none">Holly Black,<br /><br />I don't know why I haven't read more of your stuff! I've read only The Darkest Part of the Forest before this one, a year or two ago, and really liked it, so I'm not sure why it's taken me this long to pick up another of your books. My mistake! I loved the flawed characters in this one, the depth of the worldbuilding without info-dumping, the creativity. Also, thanks for making sure you put representation into your book. Some people might call it "the liberal agenda," but I'll gladly wear that intended insult as a badge of honor - fighting for diversity, inclusion, love over hate, acceptance, representation... none of those things are negatives in my book. <br /><br />Alas, this is only a standalone. Such a shame, as I'd love to see more of this world. :) Maybe a sequel in the future? :)<br /><br />Yours,<br />Steven</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xlBMzKB5wwxjsiqlgBv6S2paXZQLUQBZySu0QuwppWn3H3Y0t0iA5tf+S6MbnP8DCfkLntEARoF++mnq4UVSpg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/Rad1DGGlYWizP700R82u9C2j2nmKYnjGeWdfYW8iu3MWacsJrfWbxaAn/JKmDPzsxXZYzx4zzuuNEDViNB9Ig==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14301195971084409592">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house </span>
  <span id="freeText14301195971084409592" style="display:none">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house with a secret library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14301195971084409592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
